Or has a Buddha come to grace the morn?

Never seen this sign before—

Let's search with one mind, that's for sure.

We'll pass through thousands of millions of billions of lands,

Following the light with searching hands.

Most likely a Buddha has appeared in the world,

Come to free suffering beings, the truth unfurled.

---

Then them five hundred million billion Brahma kings, with their palaces, carrying heavenly flowers wrapped in their robes, traveled together to the northwest to track down this sign. They saw Great Universal Wisdom Excellence Tathāgata sitting at the place of enlightenment under the bodhi tree, seated on the lion throne, surrounded respectfully by gods, dragon kings, gandharvas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans and non-humans. And they saw them sixteen princes requesting the Buddha to turn the Dharma wheel.

Then them Brahma kings bowed their heads to the Buddha's feet, walked around him hundreds of thousands of times, and scattered heavenly flowers on him. The flowers they scattered piled up like Mount Sumeru, and they made offerings to the Buddha's bodhi tree. After the flower offerings, each presented their palace to the Buddha, saying:

"Please have compassion and benefit us. We offer these palaces—we hope you'll accept them."

Then them Brahma kings, right there in front of the Buddha, spoke together with one voice in verse:

Holy Master, King Among the Heavenly Ones,

Your voice like the kalavinka bird's beautiful runs,

Have compassion on all beings today,

We bow down to honor you, we pray.

World-Honored One, so rare to find,

Only appears once in a long, long time.

Through a hundred eighty ages gone by,

Empty—no Buddha in the sky.

The three evil paths are overflowing and full,

While heavenly beings diminish and dull.

Now a Buddha's appeared in this world today,

Becoming the eye for beings to see the way.

The world's place of refuge, where we all run,

Rescuing and protecting everyone.

Father of all beings, compassionate one,

Full of mercy, the blessed One.

We have this good fortune from way back when,

Now we get to meet the World-Honored One again!

---

Then them Brahma kings, after singing the Buddha's praise, each said:

"We only hope the World-Honored One will have compassion on everyone and turn the Dharma wheel to free all beings."

Then them Brahma kings spoke together with one voice in verse:

Great Holy One, turn the Dharma wheel today,

Reveal how all phenomena work and play,

Free the suffering beings from their pain,

Let them receive great joy again.

When beings hear this teaching you bring,

Some reach the Way, some to heaven they'll spring.

Evil paths will decrease and fall away,

While those who bear and practice goodness will increase each day.

Then Great Universal Wisdom Excellence Tathāgata—he just nodded silently, saying yes.

---

---

THE BUDDHA TURNS THE DHARMA WHEEL

The Buddha continued:

"Then Great Universal Wisdom Excellence Tathāgata, having received the requests from the Brahma kings of the ten directions and from them sixteen princes—right then and there, he turned the Dharma wheel three times with twelve aspects.

This is the kind of wheel that no monk or brahmin priest, no god or demon or Brahma being, nobody else in the whole world could turn. He said:

'This is suffering.

This is the arising of suffering.

This is the cessation of suffering.

This is the path to the cessation of suffering.'

And he spoke extensively about the twelve-linked chain of dependent origination:

Ignorance causes karmic formations.

Karmic formations cause consciousness.

Consciousness causes name-and-form.

Name-and-form causes the six sense bases.

The six sense bases cause contact.

Contact causes feeling.

Feeling causes craving.

Craving causes grasping.

Grasping causes becoming.

Becoming causes birth.

Birth causes old age, death, sorrow, grief, suffering, and distress.

And when ignorance ceases, karmic formations cease.

When karmic formations cease, consciousness ceases.

When consciousness ceases, name-and-form ceases.

When name-and-form ceases, the six sense bases cease.

When the six sense bases cease, contact ceases.

When contact ceases, feeling ceases.

When feeling ceases, craving ceases.

When craving ceases, grasping ceases.

When grasping ceases, becoming ceases.

When becoming ceases, birth ceases.

When birth ceases, old age, death, sorrow, grief, suffering, and distress cease.

---

"When the Buddha spoke this teaching before that great assembly of gods and humans, six hundred million billion nayuta people—because they didn't cling to any dharma—their minds were freed from all outflows. They all attained deep and wonderful meditation, the three knowledges, the six spiritual powers, and the eight liberations.

When he spoke the teaching the second time, the third time, and the fourth time, thousands of millions of billions like the sands of the Ganges River—all them beings also, because they didn't cling to any dharma, got their minds freed from all outflows.

From then on, the community of hearers was beyond measure, beyond counting—you couldn't figure out how many."

---

THE SIXTEEN PRINCES BECOME MONKS AND TEACH THE LOTUS SUTRA

"At that time, them sixteen princes all left home as young boys to become novice monks. They had sharp faculties, bright and clear intelligence. They'd already made offerings to hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of Buddhas in the past, practicing pure conduct, seeking that supreme perfect enlightenment.

Together they said to the Buddha: 'World-Honored One, all these countless thousands of millions of billions of great and virtuous hearers have already achieved realization. World-Honored One, please teach us too about the Dharma of supreme perfect enlightenment. When we hear it, we'll all practice and study it together. World-Honored One, we aspire to the Tathāgata's knowing and seeing. What's deep in our minds, the Buddha knows it himself.'

At that time, among the people that the wheel-turning holy king had brought with him, eighty million billion people saw them sixteen princes leave home, and they also asked to leave home. The king gave them permission.

---

"After that, the Buddha accepted the request of them novice monks. After twenty thousand ages passed, then before the fourfold assembly, he spoke this Mahayana sutra called the Lotus Flower of the Wonderful Dharma—the Teaching for Bodhisattvas, What the Buddha Protects and Keeps in Mind.

When he finished speaking this sutra, them sixteen novice monks—for the sake of supreme perfect enlightenment—all received it, upheld it, recited it, and penetrated it completely.

When this sutra was being taught, them sixteen bodhisattva novice monks all believed and accepted it. Among the hearer community, some also understood with faith. But other beings—thousands of millions of billions of kinds—all gave rise to doubts.

The Buddha spoke this sutra for eight thousand ages without ever resting. After finishing speaking this sutra, he went into a quiet room and entered deep meditation for eighty-four thousand ages.

During that time, them sixteen bodhisattva novice monks knew the Buddha had entered his room and was sitting in silent meditation. So each one climbed up on a Dharma seat, and for eighty-four thousand ages, for the fourfold assembly, they extensively explained and analyzed this Wonderful Dharma Lotus Flower Sutra.

Every single one of them guided six hundred million billion nayuta beings as numerous as the sands of the Ganges River. They taught them, benefited them, gladdened them, and caused them to develop the mind for supreme perfect enlightenment.

---

"After eighty-four thousand ages, Great Universal Wisdom Excellence Buddha came out of his samādhi. He went to the Dharma seat, sat down peacefully, and announced to the great assembly:

'These sixteen bodhisattva novice monks are extremely rare and precious. Their faculties are sharp and clear, their wisdom bright and penetrating. They've already made offerings to countless thousands of millions of billions of Buddhas. In the presence of those Buddhas, they constantly practiced pure conduct, receiving the Buddha's wisdom and opening it up for beings, causing them to enter into it.

You should all repeatedly draw near to them and make offerings to them. Why? Because if any hearers, solitary realizers, or bodhisattvas can believe the sutra-teaching spoken by these sixteen bodhisattvas, can accept it and not reject it—then every one of them will attain the supreme perfect enlightenment and the Tathāgata's wisdom.'"

---

THE SIXTEEN PRINCES ARE NOW BUDDHAS IN THE TEN DIRECTIONS

The Buddha told them monks:

"These sixteen bodhisattvas constantly delighted in speaking this Wonderful Dharma Lotus Flower Sutra. Each bodhisattva guided six hundred million billion nayuta beings as numerous as the sands of the Ganges River. Life after life, wherever those beings were born, they were born together with the bodhisattva, heard the teaching from him, and all believed and understood. Through this cause and condition, they encountered four hundred million billion World-Honored Buddhas, and even now it ain't finished.

Brothers, I'm telling you now: them sixteen novices who were disciples of that Buddha—they've all now attained supreme perfect enlightenment. In the lands of the ten directions, right now they're speaking the Dharma, with countless hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of bodhisattvas and hearers as their followers.

Two of them novices are Buddhas in the eastern direction. One is named Akṣobhya, in the Land of Joy. The other is named Sumeru Peak.

In the southeast direction, there are two Buddhas: one named Lion Sound, one named Lion Mark.

In the south, there are two Buddhas: one named Dwelling in Empty Space, one named Eternally Extinguished.

In the southwest, there are two Buddhas: one named Emperor Mark, one named Brahma Mark.

In the west, there are two Buddhas. One is named Amitabha. The other is named Crossing Through All Worldly Suffering and Distress.

In the northwest, there are two Buddhas: one named Tamalapattra-Sandalwood-Fragrance Spiritual Powers, one named Sumeru Mark.

In the north, there are two Buddhas: one named Cloud Freedom, one named Cloud Freedom King.

In the northeast, there's a Buddha named Destroyer of All Worldly Fear.

The sixteenth one—that's me, Śākyamuni Buddha, right here in the Saha world, having attained supreme perfect enlightenment.

---

"Brothers, when we were novice monks, each of us taught countless hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of beings as numerous as the sands of the Ganges River. They heard the Dharma from us and headed toward supreme perfect enlightenment.

Among these beings, some now dwell on the hearer ground. But I'm constantly teaching them about supreme perfect enlightenment. These people, through this Dharma, will gradually enter the Buddha Way. Why? Because the Tathāgata's wisdom is hard to believe, hard to understand.

Those countless beings like the sands of the Ganges River that we taught back then—that's you monks right here, and after I pass into final rest, the hearer disciples in the future world—that's who they are.

After I pass away, there will be other disciples who don't hear this sutra, don't know or awaken to what bodhisattvas do. Through the merit they've gained, they'll give rise to the thought of extinction and enter nirvāṇa. I'll be a Buddha in another land with a different name. Even though these people give rise to the thought of extinction and enter nirvāṇa, in that land they'll seek the Buddha's wisdom and get to hear this sutra. It's only through the Buddha Vehicle that they'll reach true extinction—there ain't no other vehicle, except when the Tathāgata uses skillful means to teach.

---

"Brothers, when the Tathāgata knows that the time for nirvāṇa has arrived, when the assembly is pure, their faith and understanding firm and solid, when they thoroughly understand the empty nature of all things and have entered deeply into meditation—then he gathers together all the bodhisattvas and hearers and speaks this sutra for them.

In this world, there's no such thing as two vehicles reaching true extinction. There's only one Buddha Vehicle that reaches true extinction.

Brothers, you should understand: the Tathāgata's skillful means penetrate deeply into the nature of beings. Knowing how they're inclined toward lesser teachings and how they're deeply attached to the five desires, for their sake he speaks about nirvāṇa. When these people hear it, they immediately believe and accept it."

---

THE PARABLE OF THE PHANTOM CITY

"Let me give you an example. Say there's a dangerous and terrible road, five hundred yojanas long, a desolate wilderness with no people, a frightening place. A big group of people wants to cross this road to get to where the treasure is.

There's a guide—smart, sharp, wise—who knows this dangerous road inside and out, knows where it's passable and where it ain't. He's leading this group of people, trying to get them through this difficult path.

But the people he's leading get tired and worn out halfway through. They say to the guide: 'We're exhausted, and we're scared too. We can't go any further. The road ahead is still so far. We want to turn back now.'

Now this guide, he's got all kinds of skillful methods. He thinks to himself: 'What a shame! How can they give up this great treasure and want to turn back?'

After thinking this, with his skillful power, on that dangerous road, after three hundred yojanas, he conjures up a great city. He tells them people:

'Don't be afraid! Don't turn back! Look—here's a big city right here where you can rest. Go in and do whatever you want. Once you enter this city, you'll be comfortable and safe. If you can push on to where the treasure is, you can go there too.'

Then them tired, exhausted people—their hearts fill up with great joy. They're amazed and say: 'Now we've escaped this terrible road! Now we're comfortable and safe!'

So all them people go into that magic city. They think they've already crossed over. They think they're safe now.

Then the guide, knowing these people have rested up and ain't tired anymore, makes that magic city disappear. He tells them:

'Come on, let's go. The place where the treasure is—it's close now. That big city back there? I conjured it up just so you could rest.'"

---

THE MEANING OF THE PARABLE

"Brothers, the Tathāgata is the same way. Right now I'm the great guide for all of you. I know that the road of birth-and-death and afflictions is dangerous, difficult, and long. You got to get away from it. You got to cross it.

If beings only heard about the One Buddha Vehicle, they wouldn't want to see the Buddha, wouldn't want to get close to him. They'd think: 'The Buddha Way is long and far. We'd have to undergo suffering for a long, long time before we could achieve it.'

The Buddha knows this mind is cowardly and inferior. Using skillful means, he teaches two kinds of nirvāṇa as a resting place midway along the road.

If beings dwell in these two stages, then the Tathāgata tells them: 'What you've done ain't finished yet. This stage where you're dwelling—it's close to the Buddha's wisdom. You should observe and consider: the nirvāṇa you've attained ain't the real thing. It's just the Tathāgata's skillful means. Within the One Buddha Vehicle, I've made distinctions and spoken of three.'

It's like that guide who, for the sake of resting, conjured up a great city. Once he knew they'd rested up, he told them: 'The treasure place is close. This city ain't real. I just conjured it up.'"

---

Then the World-Honored One, wanting to say it again, spoke it out in verse:

Great Universal Wisdom Excellence Buddha—

Ten small ages sitting at the place of the Way,

Buddha-truths wouldn't appear before him,

Couldn't complete the Buddha Way that day.

The gods, spirit-dragons, and kings,

Asuras and all their company,

Constantly rained down heavenly flowers,

Making offerings to that Buddha, you see.

The gods struck their heavenly drums,

And played all kinds of heavenly music too,

Fragrant winds blew the wilted flowers away,

And rained down fresh beautiful ones, brand new.

After ten small ages passed on by,

Then he finally achieved the Buddha Way.

Gods and humans, their hearts all leaped for joy,

Filled with happiness that glorious day.

That Buddha's sixteen sons—

Each one with their whole family tree,

Thousands of millions of billions surrounding them,

All went together to where that Buddha would be.

They bowed their heads, touching his feet,

Requested him to turn the Dharma wheel, please do.

"Holy teacher's rain of Dharma, let it fall,

Fill us up and all beings too!"

World-Honored One is so hard to meet,

Only appears once in the longest, longest while.

To awaken all the living beings,

He shakes up everything for miles and miles.

In the eastern direction's many worlds—

Five hundred million billion lands—

The Brahma palaces lit up with light,

Brighter than they'd ever seen in all them strands.

When the Brahmas saw this sign,

They came searching to find the Buddha's place,

Scattered flowers to make offerings,

Offered up their palaces with grace.

They requested the Buddha to turn the wheel,

Sang his praises in verses fine.

The Buddha knew the time wasn't right yet,

So he just sat there, accepting, giving them a sign.

From three directions and four corners too,

From up above and down below, just the same—

Scattering flowers, offering palaces,

Requesting the Buddha to turn the wheel, speaking his name.

"World-Honored One, so hard to meet!

Please, with your great compassion today,

Open wide the gate of immortal nectar,

Turn the supreme Dharma wheel, show us the way!"

That World-Honored One of boundless wisdom,

He accepted what all them people requested.

He proclaimed all kinds of teachings for them—

The Four Noble Truths, the twelve-linked chain he manifested.

From ignorance all the way to old age and death—

It all comes from birth, from being born at all.

All these faults and troubles,

Y'all should understand them, big and small.

When he proclaimed this teaching,

Six hundred million billion gai [immeasurable numbers]—

They reached the end of all suffering,

Became arhats, free from dangers.

When he spoke the Dharma the second time,

Thousands of millions like the Ganges sands,

Because they didn't cling to dharmas,

Also became arhats throughout all lands.

After that, those who reached the Way—

Their number was beyond all measure,

You could count for millions of billions of ages,

Still couldn't reach the edge of that treasure.

At that time them sixteen princes—

They left home to become novices, every one.

They all together requested that Buddha:

"Speak the Great Vehicle teaching, let it be done!

For us and all our followers,

May we all complete the Buddha Way.

May we gain what the World-Honored One has—

The wisdom-eye, first and pure, we pray."

The Buddha knew what them boys were thinking,

Knew the practices they'd done in lives gone by.

Using countless causes and conditions,

And all kinds of parables, he taught them high.

He spoke of the Six Perfections,

And all kinds of spiritual power matters.

He analyzed the real and true teachings,

The path that bodhisattvas walk and what really matters.

He spoke this Lotus Flower Sutra,

Verses numerous as the Ganges sands.

After that Buddha finished speaking,

He went to his quiet room with folded hands.

Sitting in one-pointed meditation,

For eighty-four thousand ages he stayed.

Meanwhile all them novice boys,

Knowing the Buddha in meditation hadn't yet swayed—

For countless billions of beings,

They spoke of the Buddha's supreme wisdom, clear and bright.

Each one sat on a Dharma seat,

Speaking this Great Vehicle sutra day and night.

After the Buddha came out of silence,

They preached to help spread the transformation.

Each and every one of them novices

Guided living beings—six hundred million billion, that's the calculation—

Like the sands of the Ganges River, endless and more.

After that Buddha passed into final rest,

Those who heard the Dharma from him before,

In all the Buddha-lands manifest—

They're constantly born together with their teacher.

These sixteen novices too—

They've fully walked the Buddha path,

Now dwelling in the ten directions, teaching true.

Right now they're speaking the Dharma,

Each one already perfectly enlightened.

Those who heard the teaching back then,

In all the Buddha-places, their paths brightened.

Those dwelling on the hearer ground—

I'm gradually teaching them the Buddha Way.

I was one of them sixteen back then,

And for you I spoke the Dharma in the olden days.

That's why with skillful means today,

I'm leading you toward Buddha wisdom's call.

Because of this original cause and condition,

Now I speak the Lotus Sutra to y'all.

To make you enter the Buddha Way—

Be careful, don't be frightened or dismayed!

Like a dangerous and terrible road,

Remote and far, where many dangers laid—

With vicious beasts all around,

And not a drop of water, not a blade of grass—

A place that people fear and dread,

Countless thousands of millions wanting to pass.

The road stretches out so far away—

Five hundred yojanas, the distance goes.

At that time there was one guide,

Strong in memory, with wisdom, one who knows.

His understanding clear, his mind made up,

On that dangerous path, saving folks from disaster.

But all the people got worn out and tired,

They said to that guide, their master:

"Right now we're completely exhausted,

We want to turn back from here today."

The guide thought about it, considered it:

"What a pity, what a shame, I must say!

How could they want to turn around,

And lose out on that great treasure-ground?"

Right then he thought up a skillful method,

Where his spiritual power could be found.

He conjured up a great walled city,

With decorated houses, beautiful and bright,

Surrounded by gardens and forests,

Streams and bathing pools, a lovely sight.

Double gates and tall towers,

Filled with men and women everywhere.

After he made this conjuration,

He comforted them folks: "Don't despair!

Go ahead and enter this city,

Each of you can do what brings you pleasure."

When all them people entered the city,

Their hearts filled up with joy beyond measure.

They all felt safe and secure,

Thinking: "Now we've crossed over for sure!"

The guide knew they'd rested up enough,

Gathered everyone together, that's what he was there for.

He told them: "You should keep moving on now,

This is just a conjured city here.

I saw you were exhausted,

Wanted to turn back out of fear.

So with my skillful power,

I temporarily conjured up this city wall.

Now y'all should push forward with energy—

Together we'll reach the treasure after all!"

I too am like this,

I'm the guide for everyone, you see.

I see all these seekers of the Way

Giving up halfway, unable to break free—

Unable to cross birth and death,

And all the dangerous roads of affliction too.

So with my skillful power,

I speak of nirvāṇa for rest, to help them through.

I say: "Your suffering is extinguished,

You've accomplished everything you need to do."

Once I know they've reached nirvāṇa,

All become arhats, through and through—

Then I gather the great assembly,

And speak the real truth for their sake:

The Buddhas' skillful power—

They made distinctions, spoke of three for your sake.

There's only one Buddha Vehicle,

The rest—they're just resting places, nothing more.

Now I'm telling you the real deal:

What you attained ain't the final score.

To gain the Buddha's all-knowing wisdom,

You should generate great energy and will!

When you've realized all-knowing wisdom,

The Ten Powers and all the Buddha-dharmas still—

With the thirty-two marks adorning you—

That's when you reach true extinction, nothing left to kill.

The Buddhas who are the guides,

They speak of nirvāṇa to give folks a rest on the hill.

Once they know that rest is finished,

They lead them into the Buddha's wisdom, that's the thrill."

---

END OF CHAPTER SEVEN: THE PHANTOM CITY BLUES

---

TRANSLATION NOTES:

**What We're Doing Here:**

This chapter is about time—time so vast your mind can't hold it—and about how a good teacher knows when to let tired people rest before pushing them toward the ultimate goal. I've tried to make it sing like the blues while keeping every bit of the depth.

**Key Metaphors and Choices:**

1. **The Ink and Dust Parable**: The original uses grinding earth into ink and dropping it across inconceivable distances to show how long ago this ancient Buddha lived. I kept the concrete imagery—grinding, walking, dropping—because that's what makes it real. You can feel the vastness through the physical action.

2. **The Sixteen Princes**: These are the sixteen sons who became monks, taught the Lotus Sutra, and are now Buddhas throughout the universe—including Amitabha (Pure Land) and Śākyamuni (our Buddha). This is a profound teaching about the eternal connection between teachers and students across cosmic time.

3. **The Phantom City**: This is the heart of the chapter. A guide leading exhausted travelers creates a magical rest stop—a phantom city—so they can catch their breath before continuing to the real treasure. The Buddha says this is what he does: he teaches "lesser" forms of liberation (the hearer and solitary realizer paths) as rest stops on the way to full Buddha-hood. It ain't the final destination, but it's a necessary mercy for folks who can't make the full journey all at once.

**Blues Elements Used:**

- Call and response structure in the verses

- Repetition with variation (each direction's Brahma kings)

- Direct address ("brothers," "you see," "I'm telling you")

- Concrete physical imagery (grinding, walking, raining flowers, tired feet)

- The blues truth: rest is real, exhaustion is real, but the journey ain't over

- Musical rhythm in the verse sections

- Vernacular grammar ("ain't," "gonna," "y'all")

**Theological Depth Preserved:**

This chapter teaches that the "three vehicles" (hearer, solitary realizer, and bodhisattva paths) are actually all one Buddha Vehicle—the seeming divisions are just skillful means. The Buddha creates "phantom cities" (provisional teachings) because he knows most folks can't handle the full truth right away. It's profound compassion: he meets people where they are.

The deep time framework (the ancient Buddha from countless eons ago, whose sixteen disciples are now Buddhas throughout space) shows that the Dharma operates across inconceivable dimensions—but the Buddha makes it immediate: "I see it clear as today."

**Final Word:**

The blues has always known how to carry heavy truth with a light touch, how to make the cosmic feel personal, how to honor both rest and journey. This chapter does the same thing—and I've tried to let that music come through while keeping every grain of wisdom intact.

May all beings find the rest they need and the courage to keep walking toward that treasure.

CHAPTER EIGHT: WHEN THE FIVE HUNDRED FINALLY HEARD THEIR NAMES CALLED

Blues/Gospel Vernacular Translation from Kumārajīva's Classical Chinese (406 CE)

Listen now, this is the story of how five hundred disciples found out they'd been carrying diamonds in their pockets all along.

THE PREACHER MAN FINALLY UNDERSTANDS

Now when Full Son heard all this - Full Son, that's Pūrṇa Maitrāyaṇīputra, best preacher man in the whole congregation - when he heard the Buddha laying out that wisdom, talking about how you got to meet folks where they are, speaking their language, teaching by whatever means it takes... and when he heard how the big-time disciples were getting their names called, getting told they gonna be Buddhas themselves someday... and when he heard about all the old-time connections, all that history stretching way back... and when he heard about how the Buddhas got more power and freedom than you can shake a stick at...

Man, something he never felt before washed over him. His heart got clean and jumped up in his chest. He rose right up from his seat, walked straight to the Buddha, bowed down low - put his whole face to the Buddha's feet, you know - then stepped back to one side. And he stood there looking at the Buddha's face, couldn't take his eyes off him for nothing. And he thought to himself:

"Lord have mercy, this World-Honored One is something else entirely. What he does is rare as hen's teeth. He knows how to reach all kinds of different folks, all their different ways of being. He's got this skillful knowing, this way of seeing, and he teaches to match it. He pulls people out of all the places they get stuck, all the things they grasp onto that keep 'em trapped. We can't even put words to all the Buddha's done. Only the Buddha himself knows what we been carrying deep down in our hearts all along, what we been wishing for since before we can remember."

THE BUDDHA CALLS OUT HIS BEST PREACHER

Now the Buddha turned to all the monks and said: "Y'all see this Full Son, this Pūrṇa Maitrāyaṇīputra? I been saying it all along - among all the folks who can preach, he's number one. Nobody better. And I always been talking about all the different kinds of good he does - how hard he works, how he protects and holds up the teaching, how he helps me spread this Dharma. When it comes to teaching the four kinds of followers, he shows 'em the way, he teaches 'em right, he benefits 'em, he brings 'em joy. He can break down the Buddha's true teaching every which way, and he brings real benefit to everybody walking this holy path with him. Besides the Tathāgata himself, ain't nobody can match his way with words."

"Now don't y'all go thinking Full Son only been helping me preach my Dharma. No sir. He been doing this work with ninety billion Buddhas in the past - protecting and helping spread the Buddha's true teaching. And among all those preacher men with all those Buddhas, he was number one there too. And when it comes to those Buddhas teaching about emptiness, about how things don't have any fixed self - Full Son understood that clear as day, understood it all the way through. He got what they call the four unobstructed wisdoms. He could always preach steady and clean and clear, no doubts, no hesitation. He had all the Bodhisattva's supernatural powers. All through his life, however long he lived, he walked that pure holy path. The people in those Buddha-times, they all thought he was just a hearer-disciple, just a śrāvaka. But Full Son was using that as a skillful means, you understand, and through it he benefited hundreds of thousands of beings beyond counting. And he helped countless folks without number to establish themselves on the path to supreme perfect enlightenment. Because he wanted to purify Buddha-lands, he was always doing Buddha-work, always teaching and transforming beings."

"Now listen, monks - Full Son was the number one preacher among the seven Buddhas before me. And right now with me, he's number one among those who preach. And in the coming age, the good age to come with all its Buddhas - he gonna be number one among the preachers then too. And in every case, he gonna be protecting and helping spread the Buddha's Dharma. And in the future, he gonna keep on protecting and helping spread the Dharma of countless Buddhas beyond measure - teaching and benefiting beings without number, helping 'em establish themselves on the path to supreme perfect enlightenment. Because he wants to purify Buddha-lands, he gonna keep working hard, teaching and transforming beings, little by little fulfilling the whole Bodhisattva path."

"After countless, immeasurable, infinite ages pass, right here in this land he gonna attain supreme perfect enlightenment. His name gonna be Dharmaprabha Tathāgata - that means Dharma-Light Buddha. And he gonna have all ten titles: Tathāgata, Arhat, Perfectly Enlightened One, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Unsurpassed One, Tamer of Beings, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One."

THE LAND WHERE LAW-LIGHT BUDDHA GONNA REIGN

Now his Buddha-land gonna include three thousand great thousand worlds - as many as the sands in the Ganges River - all rolled into one Buddha-land. The ground gonna be made of seven kinds of precious things. The land gonna be flat as the palm of your hand - no mountains, no valleys, no streams running through ravines, no ditches. Gonna be pavilions and towers made of seven precious things filling up that whole place. The palaces where the gods live gonna be floating right there in the sky, close by. Heaven and earth gonna meet, people and gods gonna see each other face to face.

Won't be no evil paths there - no hell, no hungry ghosts, no animals suffering. Won't be no women there either. Every being gonna be born by transformation - just appear, you know. Won't be no sexual desire. They gonna have great supernatural powers. Their bodies gonna shine with light. They gonna fly around free as birds. Their will gonna be strong and steady. They gonna be full of effort and wisdom. Every single one gonna be golden-colored and marked with the thirty-two signs that show their dignity.

The beings in that land gonna eat two kinds of food. First kind: joy in the Dharma - that's law-food, teaching-food, truth-food. Second kind: the happiness that comes from meditation - that's the food you eat when you sit still and touch what's real. There gonna be countless thousands of myriads of millions of Bodhisattvas beyond measure - they gonna have great supernatural powers and the four unobstructed wisdoms, and they gonna be good at teaching all different kinds of beings. And the hearer-disciples there, you can't even count 'em - no arithmetic, no calculation can reach that number. Every one of 'em gonna have the six supernatural powers, the three clear knowledges, and the eight liberations complete.

That Buddha-land gonna be accomplished and adorned with countless limitless virtues like these. The age gonna be called Jewel-Bright. The country gonna be called Good-and-Pure. That Buddha gonna live for countless, limitless ages beyond measure. The true Dharma gonna last way longer than that. And the reflection of the Dharma - what we call the image-age - gonna last twice as long again. When the Dharma finally disappears, the gods and humans gonna grieve.

NOW THE BUDDHA GONNA SAY IT IN VERSE

Then the World-Honored One, wanting to say all this again, spoke in verse:

Monks, you better listen close,

to the road the Buddha's children chose.

They learned the skillful way so well,

it's beyond what thinking's mind can tell.

They knew the crowd just wanted small,

they feared the wisdom's great big call.

So all those Bodhisattvas there

played the part of disciples everywhere -

Acting like hearers, acting small,

using countless means to reach 'em all.

They said, "We just disciples be,

from Buddha-way we're far as far can be."

But they delivered countless souls,

made 'em whole, fulfilled their roles.

Though people lazy, wanting less,

slowly they'd lead 'em to Buddha-ness.

Inside they kept the Bodhisattva way,

outside they looked like disciples day to day.

Seemed like they had small desires, hated birth and death,

but really they were purifying Buddha-lands with every breath.

They'd show themselves with greed and hate and ignorance,

they'd even show themselves with views that didn't make sense.

My disciples work like this, you see,

with skillful means they set folks free.

If I told you everything,

all the shapes that they could bring,

all the ways they'd transform and change,

folks would hear and think it strange -

They'd have doubts fill up their mind.

But now, this Full Son, understand,

with thousands of billions of Buddhas in ancient times,

he walked the path, he climbed and climbed,

He preached and he protected every Buddha's law,

seeking that highest wisdom that he saw.

With all those Buddhas, there he stood,

showing he's a disciple, learned and good.

He preached without a single fear,

making all the crowd glad to hear.

He never got tired, never got worn down,

helping Buddha's work in every town.

He done crossed over, got his supernatural powers complete,

got the four unobstructed wisdoms, neat.

Knew which folks were sharp, which ones were slow,

always preached the pure Dharma, made it flow.

Explaining meanings clear as clear can be,

teaching thousands of billions, setting 'em free,

making 'em dwell in the Great Vehicle way,

and purifying his own Buddha-land, day by day.

In the future too, he gonna serve

countless Buddhas, never gonna swerve.

Protecting, helping, preaching what is true,

and purifying his Buddha-land too.

Always using skillful means everywhere,

preaching the Dharma without fear.

He gonna save more folks than you can measure,

help 'em all reach wisdom's treasure.

Making offerings to all the Tathāgatas bright,

protecting the Dharma-treasure day and night.

After that, he gonna become a Buddha too,

his name Law-Bright - Dharmaprabha, that's who.

His country called Good-Pure, you see,

made of seven precious things in harmony.

His age called Jewel-Bright and fair,

Bodhisattvas everywhere -

Countless billions beyond all measure,

crossed over with supernatural power beyond treasure,

威威德德力力具具足足，，

filled with awesome virtue and might,

covering that whole land with light.

Hearer-disciples countless there,

with three clear knowings and liberations eight so rare,

got four unobstructed wisdoms complete -

these gonna be the congregation he gonna meet.

All the beings in that nation,

done cut off sexual inclination.

Every one born by pure transformation,

with fine marks adorning their formation.

They gonna eat joy-in-law and meditation-bliss,

won't think of any other food but this.

Won't be no women anywhere,

won't be no evil paths there.

Full Son the monk, you understand,

got all his virtues filled out grand.

He gonna get this pure land here,

with wise and holy folks so dear.

Countless things like this there be,

but I just told it briefly.

THE TWELVE HUNDRED START HOPING

Now at that time, those twelve hundred arhats - the ones who done got their minds free - they was thinking: "We're so happy, we ain't never felt nothing like this before. If the World-Honored One would call our names one by one, give us our prophecies like he done for those other big-time disciples, wouldn't that be something sweet?"

The Buddha knew what they was thinking in their hearts. He turned to Mahākāśyapa - that's Great Kāśyapa - and said: "I'm gonna call these twelve hundred arhats' names right here and now, one after another, and give 'em their prophecies of supreme perfect enlightenment."

"Now in this congregation here, my great disciple Ājñāta-Kauṇḍinya - that's Understanding-Chen-Ru - he gonna make offerings to sixty-two thousand billion Buddhas, and after that, he gonna become a Buddha himself. His name gonna be Samantaprabha Tathāgata - that's Universal-Light Buddha. And he gonna have all ten titles: Tathāgata, Arhat, Perfectly Enlightened One, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Unsurpassed One, Tamer of Beings, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One."

"And those five hundred arhats - Uruvilva-Kāśyapa, Gaya-Kāśyapa, Nadi-Kāśyapa, Kālodayin, Udāyin, Aniruddha, Revata, Kapphina, Bakkula, Cunda, Svāgata, and the rest - every single one of 'em gonna attain supreme perfect enlightenment. Every one of 'em gonna share the same title, all gonna be called Samantaprabha - Universal-Light."

NOW THE BUDDHA GONNA SAY IT IN VERSE AGAIN

Then the World-Honored One, wanting to say this meaning again, spoke in verse:

Understanding-Chen-Ru monk gonna see

countless Buddhas endlessly.

After ages past all measure time,

he gonna reach enlightenment's peak and climb.

Always gonna send out great big light,

filled up with supernatural powers and might.

His name gonna be famous through every direction,

everyone gonna give him respect and affection.

Always gonna preach the highest way,

that's why they call him Universal-Light, they say.

His Buddha-land gonna be pure and clean,

Bodhisattvas brave like you ain't never seen.

They gonna climb up wonderful towers high,

travel to worlds in every part of the sky,

with offerings supreme beyond all telling,

presenting them to Buddhas in every dwelling.

After they done made these offerings complete,

their hearts filled up with joy so sweet,

in just a moment they gonna fly back home -

that's the kind of supernatural power they own.

That Buddha gonna live sixty thousand ages long,

the true Dharma gonna last twice that song.

The image-Dharma twice that time again,

when the Dharma dies, gods and humans feel the pain.

Those five hundred monks, you understand,

one by one gonna become Buddhas in this land.

All of 'em gonna share the name Universal-Light,

taking turns getting prophecies, that's right.

"After I done passed away," the Buddha said,

"So-and-so gonna be a Buddha instead.

The world that he gonna teach and transform there

gonna be just like mine everywhere.

The purity of that Buddha-land,

the supernatural powers so grand,

the Bodhisattvas and hearers he gonna teach,

the true Dharma and image-Dharma's reach,

How long his life gonna measure out -

all gonna be like what I been talking about.

Kāśyapa, now you done learned and know

about these five hundred who done been freed to go.

As for all the other hearer-disciples here,

they gonna be just like this, that's clear.

Those who ain't in this meeting today,

you gotta go and tell 'em what I say."

THE JEWEL SEWN IN THE ROBE - THE HEART OF IT ALL

Now when those five hundred arhats got their prophecies called out right there in front of the Buddha, they was so happy they was jumping up and down. They rose up from their seats, went right to the Buddha, bowed down with their faces to his feet, and they confessed, they repented, they held themselves accountable:

"World-Honored One, we been thinking all this time that we done reached the final destination, that we'd got to ultimate liberation. But now we see we was like folks with no sense, no wisdom at all. Why we say that? Because we should've got the Tathāgata's wisdom, but instead we settled for small wisdom and thought that was enough."

"World-Honored One, it's like this - it's like there was a man, and he went to his good friend's house. This was a close friend, a real friend. And he got drunk and passed out, just fell out sleeping. Now his friend, he had some official business he had to take care of, had to go handle something. So before he left, he took a priceless jewel - I mean priceless, worth more than you can count - and he sewed it into the lining of his friend's robe. Just sewed it right in there and left."

"Now that man, he was passed out drunk, didn't know nothing about it, didn't feel a thing. When he woke up, he hit the road, started traveling around, went to another country altogether. And he had to scrape for food, scrape for clothes to wear. He was working hard, straining and struggling, having it real rough. And if he managed to get just a little bit of something, he figured that was enough. He'd settle for that."

"Later on, that good friend happened to run into him and saw him living like this. And he said: 'Man! Brother! Why you out here struggling for food and clothes like this? Way back when, I wanted you to be comfortable, wanted you to have ease, wanted you to be able to enjoy all five kinds of pleasures however you wanted. On such-and-such a year, such-and-such a month, such-and-such a day, I sewed a priceless jewel into the lining of your robe. It's still right there! And here you are not knowing it, worrying and suffering and working yourself to death just to survive. That's foolish, man! You can take this jewel and trade it for whatever you need. You can live however you want, never have to worry about running short of nothing.'"

"The Buddha's just like that. When he was a Bodhisattva, he taught us, he helped us develop the mind that seeks all-knowing wisdom. But we forgot. We forgot all about it. We didn't know, didn't remember. When we got to the arhat path, we thought we'd reached liberation, thought we was done. Making it through life was hard. Getting a little bit seemed like enough. But that wish for all-knowing wisdom - it was still there, never lost."

"Now the World-Honored One woke us up, made us see. He said to us: 'Monks, what y'all got ain't the ultimate liberation. Long ago I had y'all plant Buddha-seeds, good roots that grow into Buddha-trees. I used skillful means to show y'all what looked like nirvāṇa, what looked like the final destination. And y'all thought you'd really reached ultimate liberation.'"

"World-Honored One, now we finally understand - we really are Bodhisattvas. We done received the prophecy of supreme perfect enlightenment. Because of this, we're happier than we ever been in our lives. This is joy we ain't never known before."

NOW THEY GONNA SAY IT IN VERSE

Then Ājñāta-Kauṇḍinya and the others, wanting to say this meaning again, spoke in verse:

We heard that highest, peaceful voice,

telling us our names - we had no choice

but to feel a joy we ain't never known,

and bow to the Buddha with wisdom full-grown.

Now here before the World-Honored One

we confess what we done and ain't done.

Though we had a share of Buddha-treasure beyond measure,

we settled for a little bit of nirvāṇa-pleasure,

Like foolish folks without good sense,

we thought that little bit was immense.

It's like a poor man, see,

went to his good friend's place to be.

That friend's house was mighty rich,

had all kinds of food, every dish.

He took a priceless jewel, you understand,

and sewed it in the poor man's robe with his own hand,

Gave it quiet-like and then was gone.

The man was sleeping, didn't know what was going on.

When that man woke up and rose,

he traveled to another country, as the story goes.

Looking for clothes and for food to get by,

scraping to survive with many a sigh.

Life was hard, so hard to bear,

if he got a little something, he thought that was rare -

He didn't wish for nothing better than that little bit.

He didn't know that right there where he sit,

sewn inside his robe's lining there

was a priceless jewel beyond compare.

The friend who gave that jewel back when,

he saw this poor man struggling again.

He scolded him hard, got after him good,

and showed him the jewel sewn in where it stood.

When the poor man saw that jewel shine,

his heart was filled with joy so fine.

He was rich! Had wealth to burn!

Could enjoy five pleasures at every turn.

We're just like that, every one.

World-Honored One, through the long dark night you done

always pitied us, always helped us see,

made us plant seeds of the highest wish to be free.

But we had no wisdom, didn't understand,

didn't know it, didn't see what was in our hand.

We got a little share of nirvāṇa, small and slight,

thought that was enough, thought we was done right.

Now the Buddha woke us up, you see,

said what we got ain't real and final and free.

When we get the Buddha's highest wisdom, that unsurpassed knowing,

only then we gonna reach real liberation's showing.

Now we done heard from the Buddha here

about prophecies and adornments, made it all clear.

And heard we gonna take our turns receiving the call,

and our bodies and minds are full of joy, one and all.

END OF CHAPTER EIGHT: WHEN THE FIVE HUNDRED FINALLY HEARD THEIR NAMES CALLED

---

TRANSLATION NOTES:

This chapter is the heart of the Lotus Sutra's democratic revelation - the moment when the "ordinary" disciples discover they've been carrying Buddha-nature all along without knowing it. The central parable of the jewel sewn into the robe is one of the most powerful images in Buddhist literature, and it speaks directly to the blues tradition's understanding of hidden dignity, forgotten promise, and the shocking grace of recognition.

**Key metaphorical choices:**

1. **"Full Son" for Pūrṇa** - His name literally means "full" (pūrṇa), and "Maitrāyaṇīputra" means "son of Maitrāyaṇī," so "Full Son" captures both elements in vernacular English that sounds natural when spoken aloud.

2. **"Preacher man"** - Pūrṇa's designation as foremost in teaching the Dharma translates naturally to the African American religious tradition's "preacher," a figure of respect and power.

3. **"Getting drunk and passing out"** - The original Chinese "醉酒而臥" is frank about intoxication. The blues tradition doesn't sanitize human weakness - it names it directly while holding space for redemption.

4. **"Scraping for food and clothes"** - The original describes arduous struggle for basic survival ("為衣食故，勤力求索，甚大艱難"). This directly parallels the blues tradition's unflinching acknowledgment of poverty and hard times.

5. **"Man! Brother! Why you out here struggling like this?"** - The original "咄哉、丈夫" is an exclamation of shock and dismay. The blues vernacular "Man! Brother!" captures that emotional directness.

6. **"I sewed a priceless jewel into the lining of your robe"** - This image is preserved exactly because it's already perfect - concrete, specific, shocking. The hidden wealth sewn into the garment of someone who doesn't know they're carrying it speaks across centuries and cultures.

7. **Rhythm and repetition** - The verse sections employ call-and-response patterns, internal rhyme, and rhythmic repetition that would work when sung or chanted. "One by one," "day by day," "that's right," "you see" - these create musical flow.

8. **Direct address** - The translation consistently uses "you" and "we," speaking person-to-person rather than lecturer-to-student, maintaining the oral tradition's intimacy.

The spiritual truth here is universal: we've been wandering in poverty thinking we're far from home, when all along we've been carrying everything we need. We settled for small blessings when infinite blessing was sewn into our very garments. The Buddha (like the true friend) doesn't give us something new - he reveals what we've had all along but forgot. This is the blues revelation: you been somebody all along, child. You just forgot. Now remember.

CHAPTER NINE: WHEN THE FAITHFUL GET THEIR DUE

(Prophecies for the Learners and the Learned)

Now Ānanda and Rāhula, they been sitting there watching all these prophecies going out, and something starts stirring in their hearts. They thinking to themselves: "We been here all along, ain't we? Don't we get a word too? Wouldn't that be something—wouldn't that be sweet?"

So they rise up from where they sitting, and they walk right up to the Teacher, and they bow down low, faces to his feet, showing proper respect. And together they speak up:

"World-Honored One, we been thinking—we got a place in this too, don't we? Ain't nobody else we can turn to but you, Lord. You the only one. And everybody knows us—all the heavenly beings and earthly folk, even the demons know who we are. Ānanda here, he been standing by your side, keeping watch over every word you spoke, holding the teaching safe like a mama holds her baby. And Rāhula, well, he your own flesh and blood, your actual son. So if you gonna speak that supreme enlightenment over us, if you gonna call our names too—well, that would fill up what we been hoping for. That would satisfy what all these people been expecting. Our cup would overflow, and the crowd's cup too."

Now there was two thousand disciples in that assembly—some still learning, working it out, still on the journey; some already graduated, got their lessons down. And when they heard Ānanda and Rāhula speak up, every last one of them rises to their feet. They slip their right shoulder out of their robes—that's the way you show respect—and they come forward to the Buddha, and they put their palms together, and they just stand there looking up at him with one heart, one hope, same desire Ānanda and Rāhula got. Just standing there on the side, waiting. Patient people. Faithful people. Been there all along.

Then the Buddha, he turns to Ānanda and he says:

"Ānanda, listen now. In the world that's coming, you gonna become a Buddha. They gonna call you Mountain-Sea-Wisdom-Free-Penetration-King Tathāgata, Worthy of Offerings, Perfectly Enlightened One, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Unsurpassed One, Tamer of Beings, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One.

"You gonna serve sixty-two billion Buddhas, gonna keep watch over the teaching for every one of them, protecting that Dharma like you been protecting mine. And after all that faithful service, after all that holding and keeping and remembering—then you gonna reach that supreme perfect enlightenment your own self.

"You gonna teach twenty thousand million billion Ganges-river-sands worth of bodhisattvas, gonna bring them all the way up to that supreme perfect enlightenment. Your land gonna be called Constant-Victory-Banner-Standing—and child, that land gonna be clean. Pure as pure can be. The ground gonna be lapis lazuli, that deep blue stone, smooth and precious. And the era you teaching in, they gonna call it Wonderful-Sound-Pervading, 'cause your voice gonna fill everything, gonna reach everywhere.

"Your life as a Buddha gonna last countless thousands of millions of billions of immeasurable eons—you can't even count it. You could spend a thousand million billion immeasurable eons trying to calculate it with your finest mathematics, and you still couldn't get the number. The true Dharma gonna last twice as long as your lifetime. The reflected Dharma gonna last twice as long as the true Dharma.

"And Ānanda, this Mountain-Sea-Wisdom-Free-Penetration-King Buddha—that's you, child—you gonna be praised by innumerable thousands of millions of billions of Ganges-sands worth of Buddhas in all ten directions. They all gonna be singing your name, speaking your merit, telling what you done."

Then the World-Honored One, he wants to make sure this truth sinks down deep, so he sings it out in verse, makes it a song they can remember:

Right here in this assembly, I'm speaking it plain:

Ānanda, who holds the Dharma like a vessel holds rain,

You gonna serve the Buddhas, every one that you meet,

Then you gonna wake up perfect, gonna claim your own seat.

They'll call you Mountain-Sea-Wisdom, Self-Mastered-King,

Your land gonna be spotless, purest precious thing,

Called Constant-Victory-Banner, that's the name of your ground,

You gonna teach bodhisattvas thick as stars all around.

Countless as the Ganges sand, that's how many you'll raise,

Your Buddha-power gonna be mighty, your reputation gonna blaze,

Your name gonna fill ten directions, everywhere they gonna know,

Your lifetime can't be measured—mercy makes it overflow.

You gonna live so long, child, out of love for what you teach,

True Dharma gonna last double that, extending your reach,

And the reflected Dharma, it gonna double that again—

Like Ganges-river-sandgrains, countless people you'll bring in.

All those innumerable beings gonna plant their seeds

In this Buddha-Dharma of yours, gonna meet their deepest needs,

They gonna start their journey to Buddhahood right there,

In the field you tended faithful, with your patient care.

Now there was eight thousand bodhisattvas in that gathering who just recently started out on the path, beginners really, and they looking at all this and they start wondering. They thinking to themselves: "Hold on now—we ain't even heard the great bodhisattvas, the advanced ones, getting prophecies like this. So what's the reason, what's the cause, that these voice-hearers, these disciples, getting such clear predictions?"

The World-Honored One, he knows what they thinking—he can read a heart like you read a book. So he speaks to them directly:

"Good sons, listen here. Me and Ānanda, we made our vows together way back when, under the Buddha called Empty-King. We both set our hearts on that supreme perfect enlightenment at the same time, same place.

"But Ānanda, he always loved learning. He wanted to hear it all, study it all, remember it all. Me, I went the route of vigorous practice, constant pushing, hard work, discipline. That's why I already reached that supreme perfect enlightenment, and Ānanda—he been protecting my teaching, keeping the Dharma safe. He gonna protect the Dharma-treasure of all the Buddhas coming in the future too. He gonna teach and bring to completion multitudes of bodhisattvas.

"That was his original vow, you see. That was his heart's desire from way back. That's why he gets this prophecy now. He been faithful to his calling."

Now Ānanda, standing right there before the Buddha, hearing his own name called, hearing about that pure land that's coming, hearing every single thing he ever hoped for being confirmed—his heart just fills up. Joy like he never known before washes over him. It's unprecedented. Never felt nothing like it.

And right then, in that moment, he remembers. He remembers the Dharma-treasures of countless thousands of millions of billions of Buddhas from the ancient past. All of it comes flooding back, and he understands it perfectly, no obstacles, clear as day—just like what he hearing right now. And he understands his original vow too. He remembers who he always been.

So Ānanda, he sings out his own verse:

World-Honored One, you so rare, so precious, so unique—

You made me remember the past, made the ancient present speak,

All those countless Buddha-teachings from so long ago

Coming back clear as today, now I finally know.

I ain't got no doubts no more, I'm settled on this road,

I'm standing firm in Buddha-way, carrying this load,

I played my part with skillful means, standing by your side,

Protecting all the Buddhas' Dharma, faithful as a bride.

Then the Buddha turns to Rāhula and he says:

"Rāhula, in the world to come, you gonna become a Buddha. They gonna call you Stepping-on-Seven-Jewel-Flowers Tathāgata, Worthy of Offerings, Perfectly Enlightened One, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Unsurpassed One, Tamer of Beings, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One.

"You gonna serve Buddhas numbering like the dust-motes in ten worlds, and you gonna always be the eldest son to all of them, just like you are to me right now. Always the firstborn. Always that close.

"This Stepping-on-Seven-Jewel-Flowers Buddha—the purity of your land, how long you gonna live, how long the era lasts, how many disciples you gonna teach, the true Dharma period, the reflected Dharma period—all of it gonna be just like Mountain-Sea-Wisdom-Free-Penetration-King Tathāgata. No different. And you gonna be the eldest son to that Buddha too, before you step into your own enlightenment and become a Buddha yourself."

Then the World-Honored One sings it in verse so they won't forget:

When I was a prince in the palace, living that royal life,

Rāhula was my firstborn son, before all the strife,

Now I've awakened to Buddha-way, and he's my son in Dharma too,

Receiving the teaching, carrying it on, loyal and true.

In the ages yet to come, he gonna see billions of Buddhas rise,

Gonna be the eldest son to every one, that's his prize,

Single-hearted, seeking Buddha-way with everything he got,

Faithful to that one true path, never forgot.

Rāhula practices in secret, hidden deep inside,

Only I can see it, only I know what he hides,

Right now he shows himself as my eldest son for all to see,

Teaching these multitudes by his example, humble as can be.

Billions and billions of merit, countless virtues he done stored,

Settled firm in Buddha-Dharma, seeking that supreme reward,

Standing steady on the path, walking toward that highest light,

Patient as the morning, faithful as the night.

Now the World-Honored One, he looks out at those two thousand people—learners and learned, still-training and beyond-training—and he sees that their hearts are soft now, quiet and clean, peaceful and pure, all of them looking at him with one mind, one gaze.

The Buddha says to Ānanda: "You see these two thousand people—the learners and the learned?"

Ānanda says: "Yes, Lord, I see them."

"Ānanda, every single one of these people gonna serve Buddhas numbering like the dust-motes in fifty worlds. They gonna honor them, respect them, protect the Dharma-treasure for every one.

"And then, at the end, they all gonna become Buddhas at the same time, in the same moment, in lands throughout the ten directions. And they all gonna have the same name—every last one. They gonna be called Jewel-Mark Tathāgata, Worthy of Offerings, Perfectly Enlightened One, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Unsurpassed One, Tamer of Beings, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One.

"They all gonna live for one eon. The purity of their lands, the number of voice-hearers and bodhisattvas, the true Dharma period, the reflected Dharma period—all of it gonna be exactly equal, exactly the same. No difference between them. All equal. All honored."

The World-Honored One sings it again to make it stick:

These two thousand voice-hearers standing here today,

I'm giving prophecy to every one, showing them the way,

In the future they gonna become Buddhas, gonna reach that goal,

After serving countless Buddhas, they gonna make it whole.

They gonna serve as many Buddhas as the dustmotes I described,

Protecting the Dharma-treasure, keeping the truth alive,

After all that faithful service, they gonna wake up at last,

Gonna sit in perfect enlightenment, free from the past.

Each in their own direction, in lands spread all around,

But they gonna share one name, one title, one renown,

All sitting in the place of enlightenment at the exact same time,

All bearing witness to supreme wisdom, all in their prime.

Every one called Jewel-Mark—that's the name they'll bear,

Their countries and their students, everything they'll share,

True Dharma and reflected Dharma lasting just the same,

Equal in every measure, equal in their fame.

All of them using supernatural powers to save beings far and wide,

Their reputation spreading everywhere, reaching every side,

Gradually they gonna enter into nirvāṇa's peaceful rest,

After a lifetime of teaching, after giving their very best.

When those two thousand learners and learned ones heard the Buddha speak their prophecy, they couldn't hold it in. Joy jumped up in them, they started leaping and dancing, and they sang back to him:

World-Honored One, you a lamp of wisdom burning bright,

We heard you call our names, we heard you speak our plight,

Our hearts are overflowing, filled up to the brim,

Like we been touched by immortal nectar, like sweet dew on the rim.

END OF CHAPTER NINE: WHEN THE FAITHFUL GET THEIR DUE

---

This chapter is about the dignity of service, the honor of patience, and the vindication of the faithful. I made several key interpretive choices:

**Central Metaphors:**

- "Holding the teaching like a mama holds her baby" - for Ānanda's role as protector of the Dharma

- "Our cup would overflow" - blues/gospel language for fulfillment and satisfaction

- "Faithful as a bride" - for Ānanda's loyal devotion

- "Patient as the morning, faithful as the night" - for Rāhula's steady practice

- "Like sweet dew on the rim" - transforming "nectar" (甘露/amṛta) into something both familiar and transcendent

**Character Voices:**

- Ānanda and Rāhula speak with humility but also with legitimate desire for recognition

- The 2,000 are characterized by their patient silence and collective hoping

- The Buddha speaks with both formality (in the official prophecies with full titles) and intimacy (in explanation)

**Structural Choices:**

- Maintained the prose/verse alternation of the original

- Used verse for the Buddha's confirmations to create memorable, singable moments

- Employed repetition and rhythmic patterns characteristic of both sutras and blues ("gonna" as a future marker creates forward momentum)

- The phrase "learners and learned" preserves the original's 學無學 (those in training and beyond training) while making it accessible

**Key Teachings Preserved:**

- Ānanda chose the path of learning/remembering while Buddha chose vigorous practice

- This explains their different roles and timing of enlightenment

- Rāhula's practice is "secret" (密行) - hidden, inner work

- The 2,000 are all equal in their eventual attainment - democracy of enlightenment

- Service and waiting have their own dignity and lead to full realization

The title "When the Faithful Get Their Due" captures the chapter's essence: this is about patient people, background people, faithful servants finally receiving public acknowledgment and prophecy.

CHAPTER TEN: HONOR THE WORD-CARRIERS

(The Teachers of the Dharma)

Now at that time, the World-Honored One, he turns to Medicine King Bodhisattva, and through him he's talking to eighty thousand great beings, and he says:

"Medicine King, you see this great crowd gathered here? You see all these countless heavenly beings, dragon-kings, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, garuḍas, kinnaras, mahoragas? You see the human folks and the non-human folks? You see the monks and nuns, the lay brothers and lay sisters? You see those seeking to be voice-hearers, those seeking solitary enlightenment, those seeking the Buddha-way?

"Listen now: Every single one of these people—if they hear even one verse, even one sentence of this Wonderful Dharma Lotus Sutra while standing here before me, if they feel even one moment of joy rising in their hearts—I'm giving them all a prophecy right now. Every last one. They all gonna reach that supreme perfect enlightenment. All of them. No exceptions."

Then the Buddha says to Medicine King:

"Now let me tell you about after I'm gone, after I leave this world. If there's anybody who hears this Wonderful Dharma Lotus Sutra—even just one verse, just one sentence—and feels one moment of joy in their heart, I'm giving them that prophecy too. They gonna reach that supreme perfect enlightenment.

"And if there's people who receive and uphold this sutra, who read it, recite it, explain it to others, copy it down—even if it's just one verse—if they look at this scripture with reverence like they looking at the Buddha himself, if they make offerings with flowers, incense, necklaces, powdered incense, paste incense, burning incense, silk canopies, banners and flags, clothing, music, even just bringing their palms together in respect—

"Medicine King, you need to know: These people already served ten thousand billion Buddhas in the past. They already made great vows in the presence of all those Buddhas. Out of compassion for suffering beings, they chose to be born here in this human world. They came here on purpose."

"Medicine King, if somebody asks you, 'Which beings are gonna become Buddhas in the future?'—you should point to these people right here. Point to the ones who receive and uphold this Lotus Sutra. You should say: 'These people right here, they gonna become Buddhas in the future world. Guaranteed.'

"Why? Because if good men or good women receive even one sentence of the Lotus Sutra, if they uphold it, read it, recite it, explain it, copy it down, if they make offerings to the scripture-scroll with flowers, incense, necklaces, powdered incense, paste incense, burning incense, silk canopies, banners and flags, clothing, music, bringing their palms together in reverence—

"These people deserve the respect of the whole world. You should honor them the same way you honor the Buddha himself. You need to know: This person is a great bodhisattva. They already accomplished that supreme perfect enlightenment. Out of pity for suffering beings, they chose to be born here in this world to widely proclaim and explain this Wonderful Dharma Lotus Sutra.

"How much more so for someone who can receive the whole thing, who makes all kinds of offerings? That person is beyond measure."

"Medicine King, you need to understand something: These people gave up their clean, pure rewards. After I'm gone, out of compassion for suffering beings, they chose to be born in this evil world just to spread this sutra far and wide.

"If a good man or good woman, after I'm gone, can secretly teach even one person even one sentence of the Lotus Sutra—you need to know this person is sent by the Buddha himself. The Buddha dispatched them. They're doing the Buddha's own work.

"How much more so for someone who teaches it broadly to the crowds?"

"Medicine King, listen to this: If there's an evil person with a bad heart who stands before the Buddha for a whole eon—a whole cosmic age—and constantly curses the Buddha, insults him, speaks against him—well, that sin is still relatively light.

"But if somebody speaks even one evil word, one bad word, against someone who reads and recites the Lotus Sutra—whether they're a monk or a laywoman, whether they left home or still got a home—if you badmouth a teacher of this sutra, that sin is far, far heavier. You hear me? Far heavier."

"Medicine King, anyone who reads and recites the Lotus Sutra—you need to know this person is adorned with the Buddha's own adornment. They're carried on the Buddha's own shoulders. The Buddha himself is carrying them.

"Wherever they go, you should turn toward them and bow. You should bring your palms together with single-minded focus. You should honor them, serve them, respect them, praise them. Offer them flowers, incense, necklaces, powdered incense, paste incense, burning incense, silk canopies, banners and flags, clothing, fine food, make music for them. Bring them the best offerings that humans can bring, the finest you got. You should scatter heavenly treasures on them. You should present them with collections of heavenly jewels.

"Why? Why all this honor?

"Because this person joyfully teaches the Dharma. If you hear them for just a moment, just a little while, you immediately reach the ultimate—that supreme perfect enlightenment. That's why."

At that time, the World-Honored One, wanting to say this again so it sinks down deep, sings it out in verse:

If you want to walk the Buddha-road,

If you want to gain that natural wisdom-load,

You better constantly make offerings, I'm telling you true,

To those who receive and uphold this sutra, through and through.

If you want to quickly gain

All-wisdom, that's the highest plane,

You should receive and hold this scripture tight,

And honor those who hold it day and night.

If there's anybody who can receive and uphold

This Wonderful Dharma Lotus Sutra of old,

You need to know they're sent by the Buddha himself,

Came here out of pity for suffering, not for wealth.

Those who can receive and uphold this teaching here,

This Wonderful Dharma Lotus Sutra so dear,

They left their pure lands behind, you see,

Came to this world out of compassion, born to set us free.

You need to know people like this,

They got freedom to be born wherever they wish,

They can choose to come to this evil world,

To widely proclaim this supreme Dharma, let it be unfurled.

You should make offerings with heavenly flowers and incense sweet,

Heavenly jeweled clothing, lay it at their feet,

Heavenly collections of wonderful treasures, the finest kind,

To honor those who teach this Dharma to humankind.

After I'm gone, in that evil world to come,

If there's anybody can uphold this sutra, even some,

You should bring your palms together and bow down low,

Honor them like you honor the World-Honored One, you know.

Bring them the finest food, the sweetest tastes,

All kinds of clothing, nothing gone to waste,

Make offerings to this child of Buddha with everything you got,

Hoping just to hear them teach a little, just a single thought.

If there's somebody in the future world

Who can receive and uphold this sutra that's been unfurled,

I'm sending them among the people, that's where they belong,

To carry on the Buddha's work, to sing the Buddha's song.

If for a whole eon long

Somebody harbors a heart that's wrong,

Makes ugly faces and curses the Buddha to his face,

That person's sin is heavy, but it ain't the worst disgrace.

But if somebody reads, recites, and holds

This Lotus Sutra, precious as gold,

And you speak evil against them, even for a little bit,

That sin is heavier than the first—remember it.

If there's somebody seeking Buddha's way

Who for a whole eon, every single day,

Stands before me with palms together, praising me

With countless verses, honoring what they see—

They get immeasurable merit from praising Buddha so,

But if you praise someone who upholds this sutra, you should know,

The blessings you receive surpass even that,

They're greater than all those praises—now how about that?

For eighty billion eons long,

If you make offerings with your sweetest song,

With the finest colors, sounds, fragrances, tastes, and touches too,

To someone who upholds this sutra, honoring what they do—

After making all those offerings, precious and refined,

If you get to hear this sutra for just a moment's time,

You should rejoice and celebrate, count yourself blessed:

"I have gained great benefit today, I have truly been caressed!"

Medicine King, I'm telling you plain,

Of all the sutras I've taught again and again,

All the scriptures I've already spoken, am speaking now, will speak later on,

Among all of them, this Lotus Sutra is the jewel, the crown.

At that time the Buddha spoke again to Medicine King Bodhisattva Mahāsattva:

"The scriptures I have taught are countless—thousands, ten thousands, billions. The ones I've already spoken, the ones I'm speaking now, the ones I will speak in the future—among all of them, this Lotus Sutra is the most difficult to believe, the most difficult to understand.

"Medicine King, this sutra is the secret treasury of all the Buddhas. It's the treasure-room, the locked vault. You can't just hand it out, can't just pass it around carelessly to anybody. This is what all the Buddhas in all the worlds have guarded and protected from ancient times until now. This teaching has never been revealed openly before.

"And this sutra—even while the Buddha is still alive, still in the world, there's plenty of hatred toward it, plenty of jealousy. How much more so after the Buddha's gone?"

"Medicine King, you need to know: After the Buddha leaves this world, if there's people who can copy this sutra, uphold it, read it, recite it, make offerings to it, explain it to others—the Buddha himself will cover them with his robe. He'll wrap them up, keep them safe.

"And they'll be protected and thought of by all the Buddhas in other lands, Buddhas who are alive right now in those worlds. These people got great faith-power, great will-power, great roots of goodness.

"You need to know: These people sleep in the same room as the Buddha. The Buddha himself lays his hand on their heads. He touches them."

"Medicine King, wherever this sutra is spoken, wherever it's read, wherever it's recited, wherever it's copied down, wherever the scripture-scroll stays—in all those places you should build a stupa made of seven precious materials. Make it extremely high, extremely wide, extremely decorated and beautiful.

"You don't need to put relics in it. You hear me? No need for relics.

"Why? Because this sutra right here already contains the Buddha's whole body. The complete body is already in there.

"This stupa should receive offerings of all kinds of flowers, incense, necklaces, silk canopies, banners and flags, music and singing. People should make offerings, show reverence, honor it, praise it.

"If anybody sees this stupa, bows to it, makes offerings to it—you need to know all these people are getting close to that supreme perfect enlightenment. They're almost there."

"Medicine King, there's a lot of people—whether they left home or still got a home—who say they're walking the bodhisattva path. But if they can't see this sutra, can't hear it, can't read it, can't recite it, can't copy it, can't uphold it, can't make offerings to it—you need to know these people haven't really walked the bodhisattva path the right way. They ain't doing it properly.

"But if there's beings who hear this sutra-teaching, who truly hear it—then they know how to walk the bodhisattva path the right way.

"Any being who's seeking the Buddha-way—if they see this Lotus Sutra or hear it, and after hearing it they believe it, understand it, receive it, uphold it—you need to know this person is getting close to that supreme perfect enlightenment. They're almost home."

"Medicine King, it's like this—imagine there's a person who's thirsty, desperate for water, needs it bad. So they go up on a high plateau, a high dry place, and they start digging, searching for water, working for it.

"At first they just see dry soil, dusty dirt. They know the water's still far off, still way down there.

"But they don't give up. They keep working, keep applying effort, don't quit. After a while they start seeing damp soil, wet dirt. Then gradually they hit mud.

"Their heart becomes certain, becomes settled. They know for sure: Water's definitely close now. It's right there.

"It's the same way with bodhisattvas. If they haven't heard this Lotus Sutra, haven't understood it, haven't been able to practice and cultivate it—you need to know these people are still far from that supreme perfect enlightenment. The water's still way down there.

"But if they hear it, understand it, think about it deeply, practice and cultivate it—then you can be certain, you can know for sure they're close to that supreme perfect enlightenment. The water's right there.

"Why? Because all bodhisattvas' supreme perfect enlightenment belongs to this sutra. This sutra opens the gate of skillful means. It reveals the true mark of reality. This Lotus Sutra treasury is deep, solid, hidden, distant. Nobody can reach it on their own.

"But now the Buddha teaches it, helps beings mature, brings bodhisattvas to completion, and opens it up for them. Shows them what's been hidden."

"Medicine King, if there's a bodhisattva who hears this Lotus Sutra and gets startled, doubtful, frightened—you need to know that's a brand-new bodhisattva, just started out. That's normal for beginners.

"If a voice-hearer, a disciple, hears this sutra and gets startled, doubtful, frightened—you need to know that's someone full of pride. That's arrogance talking."

"Medicine King, if a good man or good woman wants to teach this Lotus Sutra to the four assemblies after the Buddha's gone—how should they teach it? How should they do it?

"This good man or good woman needs to enter the Buddha's room, wear the Buddha's robe, sit on the Buddha's seat. Only then should they widely teach this sutra to the four assemblies.

"What's the Buddha's room? Great compassion for all beings—that's the Buddha's room.

"What's the Buddha's robe? Gentleness and patience—that's the Buddha's robe.

"What's the Buddha's seat? The emptiness of all things—that's the Buddha's seat.

"Settle yourself in these three. Establish yourself there. Then, with a heart that doesn't slack off, doesn't get lazy, teach this Lotus Sutra to the bodhisattvas and the four assemblies. Teach it wide."

"Medicine King, when I'm in other lands, other countries, I'll send magical people, conjured-up people, to gather an audience to hear the Dharma. I'll send magical monks, nuns, laymen, laywomen to listen to the teaching.
